For I have seen a madman who, having copped.i. excised the scrofula or the head of a woman, has coped the arteries at the collar; so that so much blood has flowed out that the woman died between her hands.
And I have seen another madman who treated a stone of a sick man, and the stone was great; so that he carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and he died of it two days later.
And I must say that I have often been called to treat such cases, and I see the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and if one should attempt to cut it out, he would surely die.
And I see another case here in our land where the limb was broken, and with the bone shattered; and the physicians of our land are straining their minds to cure it, but they leave the wound open without dressing it, and leave it thus; and they command that it be left alone; and it remains so until the limb is completely healed and the bone is whole again.
I am called to come and see him, and I hasten to come and loosen the limb; and when I see it dislocated, it is calm and does not feel any pain.

The accidental cause comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of progress in this matter is if one grasps an awl, because it has a double thread, and the thread is in the flesh, and it causes the left lower eyelid to swell so much that the thread of the vein is split in two at the level of the eye; then the flesh of the cheek is elevated from the whole awl, and the pupil is dilated to one-third of its normal size.</start_of_turn>
And if the pupil returns according to what is commanded, that is good; but if not, if one takes a burr and puts it in the incision, and turns the pupil, and makes two incisions or cuts within the pupil; and if there are two incisions at each of the two angles of the incision that you have made, or if you make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as if it were the letter which has not ‘j’grische’; then hold that cheek, according to the quantity of its cost and disease, of that which teaches the pupil, and then join the two parts that are loosened, and tie with a thread of linen; then cure the rest as we have said of the mollifying medicines and the tents, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>

Of the oil of the unguent.
The unguent oil is of two kinds: one is nervous and somewhat dark in color, like pitch; the other is not nervous, but is like solidified moisture, and when touched with iron and warmed, it causes blisters. Both seem to begin to soften towards the great marrow, and spread throughout the body, covering the eyes and the light and movement of the oil.
And as for the method of the incision, if the patient puts his shoulder in its right place, then hold the eyes; then take hold of the oil with your hand, and grasp the hair with tweezers of small double curvature, and stretch it downwards; then take a needle, and put in one hair of horse, or of calf, or of ox, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle once and pierce the hair with the needle, and tie the hair with a thread and stretch it downwards, and drain at all times the surrounding area of the oil that surrounds the nail and the hair up to the root, and leave the natural discharge or secretion, if there is no crust of tears usually caused by the incision; and in no case should the oil be stretched only with the sponge and thread, as we have said; then the sponge should be wiped clean of the oil, which is the proper form:

From the issue of the oil.
When the limb is completely open without any displacement of the marrow, without any relief, if you must bind the patient; then do the same, put on bandages or a dressing to absorb, then put on oil. Indeed, make of acaice and aloe and incense and ochre, and then strain the oil, and put it on bandages and cloths; and keep the cloths if you take cloths enough soft, and double layer in three, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that there is between them; then strain by the weight of a stiff bandage that forms, and resume the dressing by absorbing in the direction of the wound; then pin the dressing and leave the oil strained for a while and night, and if the marrow softens, if you must strain it out; then pin the marrow afterwards the marrow and the nut, and if you see the oil repairing itself, that is good; if not; repeat the dressing and the cloths and the marrow and the dressing until it is healed.

De la bowe de l’oil.
The disease which is called 'alcunnati' is not fierce except for the swelling which is made in oil, resembling descending water, which is not true; and the manner in which this swelling appears is that if you make the patient sit on a chair which appears and is straight, then take hold of his head between your hands, and move him as much as you see the swelling coming down to his eyes; then either bind him tightly, and do not let him descend and break the light, and see the patient do the things as he wants; and if it does not descend spontaneously, as we have said, make a scar and it will descend like water, and the patient will see the swelling as if it were water. If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sponge and put it on the corner of the wound. That is, by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corner of the wound and the crown, until the swelling is gone; and when it comes out, distillate in hot oil mixed with honey, or in vinegar or fennel and honey, then cure with other remedies until it is healed.

From the shoulder joint downwards.

From the hardness of the jaw bones.
Many times it happens on the gums of the teeth that they become loose and the old people call them “albules”; if you support it, grasp the root and leave the socket or blood clot; then take out the blunt end of the needle, or other astringent and drying powders; and if the gum comes back after the incision, and this happens many times, if you grasp it a second time and cauterize it: if it does not come back after the cautery; these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
Des sordens.
When the teeth are assembled at the root of the jaw, between the gums, which are loose and rough; never are the teeth black and yellow and towards the front, until the corruption comes to the gum, and they are biting; if you make the patient sit between your hands, and their shoulders are against your chest, and open the jaws or the gums split open, until nothing remains; and thus do you make blackening and greenness, and yellowness and other spots, until they are cleansed; and if you remove what is at the root at the first attempt, that is good; if that is not the case, if you must repeat the second and third time, until you have everything back in place; and the teeth that have been between the jaws must have various shapes because those that you remove to drive out the teeth have other shapes than those that are left between the teeth; and these shapes and others appear to you.
It is necessary when you cure the tooth from its pain that you wait a while before retracting too much, because it must not be made to move too much; because it is a high-quality substance, so we have no excuse for retracting. When the patient is constrained to bear down, if you are certain that the tooth is loose, many times the pain will leave the patient; and care must be taken that it is neither too loose nor too tight, and make the tooth bear down; and whatever does not suffice to relieve the pain while the mischief persists, as we have already done for these scoundrels; and when you are well certain that the tooth is loose, you must gently extract it with great force to ward off the gum from all sides; then the muscle will relax on the two sides and the pincers will be fixed; and keep the patient’s chin between the knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
After that, draw out the tooth directly toward the front; and if it does not yield, take no forceps and grasp it from the root part lightly, and move it as you did before. And if the root is perceived and breaks, if you cover it with cloth, the gum or the hole will be damaged; and if the pincers are grasped too tightly, they will break from the grasp. You must moisten around the gum to soften the tooth.
And take care that you do not break it, and leave some of it, and return to the patient with the greater pain of the first. When the teeth loosen.
When teeth loosen, whether by percussion or biting, and the patient is unable to press against that which sustains them, you must treat them with restrictive medicines, which is of no avail; for if you command them to be restrained with a gold thread, for the silver thread becomes green and causes pain, but the gums do not move at all; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth coming into contact, if you take the thread and pass it double between the two front teeth, then place the teeth between the front teeth, if there are one or more, as long as you see it clearly up to the sound tooth on the other side; then resume the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand skillfully and cautiously, until it does not move; and let your thread be attached to the root of the tooth if it is unable to escape. Then hold the teeth in tension with tweezers, assemble them, and place them between the sound tooth and the one just mentioned, and keep it so that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it so that it can rest as much as possible, and if it comes loose or the thread breaks, if you strain with another thread; if it persists and serves its purpose well, and this is the form of teeth and the arrangement of the two front teeth and the two rear teeth, as you see.
And when the tooth aches, if you reset it in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let no other be between who is wise and soothing, and never make the shape of a tooth of ivory, and put it in its place or where the fault is, and strain it as we have said, and leave it so for a long time with constant tension

Des apostemes de la gorge.
There are often boils in the throat which are called "godath", and they are called by their proper name "ij amandres". And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not cured, take heed: if they are hard of little size and have a yellow colour, do not touch them with fire. And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with fire, even for the discharge of blood; but leave them as long as they are painful, and then you will take them out, or they will break by themselves; and if they are white in colour and the root is thin, if you have brought the instrument to cover them, look first whether the boils are resting and quiet. I medicated a woman with a small abscess that was not in the throat, namely one abscess of little size; and she had such a tight grip throughout the throat that she could neither breathe through the tube that was blocked, nor eat or drink, and she died because of it. And the abscess was so high that it had forced out two teeth from their sockets. I immediately took hold of this, and put one finger on the abscess, then I forced out a large piece of flesh; then I repeated the procedure in the other socket where there was no tooth, and I closed the mouth and squeezed the tongue; after that I put the finger back in the abscess, and held one part, and only a little blood escaped from the other part; and when I had stopped bleeding from the tube in the throat, the woman was able to drink water and then wine, and she did not stop vomiting from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess gradually subsided, and filled up the space that I had evacuated, as much as it would. Then I closed the abscess and cauterized it inside the throat: from that moment the abscess turned around; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to her after that.

Therefore, when medicines are applied for the semblance of dropsy called 'eclypses of medicines', and the cure does not benefit, if you observe the patient is weak or has another disease besides dropsy, as with vomiting and other things; if there is no touch of fire, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great strength and has only dropsy, and is neither too young nor too old, then one must work. Hold the patient’s right arm in your hands, and press the belly downwards towards the lower part of the belly, then take the pointed tweezers as follows: Make three incisions each about a finger’s breadth wide, and do not make them too deep so that they can reach the intestine when inserted, and do not sew them up.
Then look if dropsy is adhering to the intestines: if you suspect that it is in the intestines, make two straight incisions on the flank; and if it is due to liver disease, make the incision on the left side of the abdomen; and if it is due to bile, make it on the right side, and do not make the incision too deep so that the patient does not bleed excessively from the wound that is too weak to withstand it.
Then pierce all the leather with the instrument, and the substance, and keep your hand all the space between the leather and the bone just as when escorting the quantity of a nail or an egg shell; then pierce the bone until the space comes to the end of the tooth, and that is the cause of the pain, then withdraw the instrument, and that is the form of this instrument: And it is similar to a silver nail, and is made of iron or lead, and has on the part facing outwards a small perforation; or costs as much as one part, two parts, and three parts on one side, and one part on the other side; and the tip is cut off like a pen, and that is the form of the incision which the writers make to cut off the pen.
At the head of this lies the ailment, so that when the instrument comes to the pain, if you immediately lift it up from the instrument; empty out then one-third or half of what is in it, for if you empty out more than that which is convenient in that hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the wound, or he will vomit, or he will approach death.
but emptying out in accordance with the quantity of its virtue, and in accordance with what the instructions of the virtue say concerning the patient and his pulse; then withdraw the instrument and retain the pain, and it is retained now by the pressure which stamps the perforation that is on the socket, as I have said, that you pierce in this manner; then repeat the instrument on the other side, if you see the patient suffering from this, and withdraw a small quantity of the pain.

of boils of the hip. For I have seen most of the masters and doctors who performed circumcision to make a hole, and to force, and with all their skill; yet if the testicles escaped because there were two threads, and by chance if one sews up the lower and leaves the upper unsewn.

Regarding the retention of urine...
The retention of urine is from the obstruction of a stone, or blood clot, or bile, or worms, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the previous division.
If the urine is not discharged, and you see that the obstruction is caused by the stone which is in the kidney or the neck of the bladder, then you must command the patient to bend his knees; put the pieces of wood outside the back, extend his abdomen from the upper part of his back, and restrain the patient so that he cannot move; and thus constrain the neck of the bladder towards the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is discharged immediately.
If it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instruments which are called “syringes,” for this is the form: either of silver wire slightly blunt at the end like the beak of a bird; or the caine of a palm of a long and a half, or wire of the finest kind.
And thus it is done with the issuing of urine that if you take one and a half threads of a double, and bind one end to a chief of wool or cotton, and wind the chief through the syringe; and drain the surplus of wool and bring it up to the end of the syringe, then join the syringe with oil or butter and rosin of egg, and make the patient sit on one seat, and raise the bladder and the belly with oil moist and oily with olive oil and tepid water.
Then put the syringe smoothly into the belly, as far as it reaches the root of the belly; then double the belly upwards towards the buttocks; then draw out the syringe until it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient urinate until it is empty, for this is not done except in this order except for the fact that it is guided or it goes crooked; then hold the thread at both ends of the wool and the urine follows the wool, and then take it out again, and correct the urine;
and start the syringe again until the bladder is empty, and align the patient.

And it is easy to cure these strains until they are three years old; and after that it is more difficult in old men, and is as bad in young men as in old; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn

from the softening of the skin of the nails

Dou chastrement
The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, and for this reason I would rather not speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary for us to do so for two reasons: the first is that the patients themselves can respond when asked, and the second is that we have often had to cauterize beasts for our assistants, such as oxen and sheep and goats and others. I say therefore that cauterization is done in two ways: by traction or by incision.  In the former, we seat the beast in warm water, until the hairs are softened and limp; then we grasp them with our hand, until they are firm and we can no longer feel them.  As for cauterization of great size: it is necessary to hold the beast steady, and to press the skin of the hairs with our left hand; then to bind the suspension, and to grasp each hair with our thumb and index finger, when they are well secured; and leave no trace of blood or clot on the vessels.  This method of cauterization is milder than that which is done by traction, because at traction the beast desires to move; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Hermofrodie est selonc deux manieres: l’une si est que entre les deux coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine. Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et deux coions. Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.
Hermaphroditism is in accordance with two manners: one if between the two testicles opens as with the figure of female nature, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine of the female. And the other manner if it is in women, and has on the navel as with a girl and two testicles. And the cure for the tumour and fame is if you cut off all the testicle stones, and the cure is like for other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine spurts through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene is a stone that is cast above the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have it as much as a hand, and this is the cure. It is necessary to keep the excess of the tenticle away from your hand or elbow, and to cut it lightly; and do not be too violent, for blood does not come, then the cure will be like for other wounds; and at another time when it appears at the mouth of the marrow, and the pain, and by chance spur out, and is like the semblance of a cow, and for this reason it is called the ancient "lame disease". If it is necessary to cut it out, as we have said concerning the tenticle, and the cure will be when it is healed.
De erratique.
If the nature of the woman is not clearly understood, or if the opening is small; and if it is natural birth, or by accident through illness, or by pressure of the bladder, or by stones in the belly, or by any other similar cause; and if the conception, and the birth, and by chance the flowers have come; and if you have knowledge of this, if the period is close to appearing, if there are two eggs in the belly, or on the side. If it is a soft swelling and is close to the genitals, if there are two testicles close to each other, put the two thumbs together, let the woman lie on her back, spread her legs; then the two testicles will form, as long as the soft swelling is round, and is over the swelling; then take oil, and pour it over the wound, and put it on the body, and keep the woman still in every place where she can’t move. And if the swelling is hard and thick, if you must break it like a hazelnut leaf. If the swelling is of the bladder, if you suspect it at the navel and break it; have medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon’s blood, incense, together with many eggs; then mix in a large dose of lard, so that the wound cannot bleed; and let it be long, and mix in a little attempt of dry lint. And if there is a stone in the belly, if you cover it according to this method, except for an inflamed appendix. For an inflamed appendix that is in the belly, do not touch it with fire.
Des emorroides.
Emorroids are openings of veins which without support are usually not accustomed; and when old, they become swollen; and as we have said in the division, their signs and symptoms, I will say here those which resolve cure. I say that emorroids and swellings, when pressed into the marrow, are not felt, except by the cure with iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the testicles tightly, grasp the head in its roots, then sprinkle over medicines which restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then close the wound an hour later, then put it into cold water; and if there is still bleeding, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and elderberry and similar things, and then take oatmeal, and mix it with honey and assails, and make one application upon her back. And if it stops, that is good. If not, if there is a wound at the back, and there are clots, take lint, and moisten it with the juice of plantain or with the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make it bleed. And when the wound is healed, if it is a swelling which is called “albathir,” it is red, and is similar to a rough beard, if you cover it as I have said the swelling; and then it will heal as well.

From infancy.
From infancy. The midwife first notes when the child naturally assumes the normal posture of an infant, and these signs are when you see the woman pressing down on the navel, and longing to smell urine: immediately the child bursts with desire to suck; so that his hands that were previously clenched now rest open, and when you see these signs, if you gently press his abdomen, if the child sucks his thumb, that is normal; for when he descends on his navel, if he remains with his thumb, he is overcome by the disgust of his superfluousness; and this is not natural. For it never happens from his toes, but from the stiffness of the limbs, or the hands, or from his belly, or from within, and is converted by chance from his collar, and from other vicious figures; if the midwife is skilled in this matter and subtle in these things, and avoids error and deception, and I will show you all the figures that help her.

...of the fracture of the arm.
The arm consists of three bones, which are called the "radius" and the "ulna". One is small and is like a nail which supports the pouch; the other is large and is like a weight, over the small thumb. Sometimes only the large bone breaks, or sometimes both; and sometimes the bones break together.
When the small bone breaks, the restoration is easy, and the healing; but when the large bone breaks, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when they break together. If only the small bone breaks, if the limb is gently extended and made even.
And if it is the large bone that breaks, if the limb is more strongly constrained; and it is extended over the thumb, and the pouch of the hand is held higher than the other, and the small bone is held lower than the others, and the patient’s hand is crossed over itself, and the thumb is above the hand, more than the patient suffers any pain; then extend the limb from the shoulder to the wrist, or from the elbow, and another limb from the other side, and then set the bones even, according to their best form.

Of the dislocation of the shoulder.
The shoulder is dislocated only in two ways: first, when it slips from the socket towards the outside; and second, when it slips from the outside towards the inside; and sometimes it slips from above, and this is bad indeed

The dislocation of the hand
The dislocation of the hand: the joint of the hand is loosened, and its return is laborious, more so than any other joint in the body. It is necessary to restore it to its place immediately, even if it is loosened, and even if there is swelling or a wound.
